interface for sending a batch of samples to an\n404: // external timeseries database.\n405: type WriteClient interface {\n406: \t// Store stores the given samples in the remote storage.\n407: \tStore(ctx context.Context, req []byte, retryAttempt int) (WriteResponseStats, error)\n408: \t// Name uniquely identifies the remote storage.\n409: \tName() string\n410: \t// Endpoint is the remote read or write endpoint for the storage client.\n411: \tEndpoint() string\n412: }\n413: \n414: // QueueManager manages a queue of samples to be sent to the Storage\n415: // indicated by the provided if you also lock seriesMtx, take seriesMtx first.\n447: \tseriesSegmentIndexes map[chunks.HeadSeriesRef]int\n448: \n449: \tshards      *shards\n450: \tnumShards   int\n451: \treshardChan chan int\n452: \tquit        chan struct{}\n453: \twg          sync.WaitGroup\n454: \n455: \tdataIn, dataOut, dataOutDuration *ewmaRate\n456: \n457: \tmetrics  *queueManagerMetrics\n458: \tinterner *pool\n459: }\n460: \n461: // NewQueueManager builds a new QueueManager and starts a new\n462: // WAL watcher with queue manager as the WriteTo destination.\n463: // The WAL watcher takes the dir parameter as the base directory\n464: // for where the WAL shall be located. Note that the full path to\n465: // the WAL directory will be constructed as <dir>/wal.\n466: func NewQueueManager(\n467: \tmetrics *queueManagerMetrics,\n468: \twatcherMetrics *wlog.WatcherMetrics,\n469: \treaderMetrics *wlog.LiveReaderMetrics,\n470: \tlogger *slog.Logger,\n471: \tdir string,\n472: \tcfg config.QueueConfig,\n473: \tmCfg config.MetadataConfig,\n474: \texternalLabels labels.Labels,\n475: \trelabelConfigs []*relabel.Config,\n476: \tclient WriteClient,\n477: \tflushDeadline time.Duration,\n478: \tinterner *pool,\n479: \tsm ReadyScrapeManager,\n480: \tenableExemplarRemoteWrite bool,\n481: \tenableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite bool,\n482: \tenableTypeAndUnitLabels bool,\n483: \tprotoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg,\n484: ) *QueueManager {\n485: \tif logger == nil {\n486: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n487: \t}\n488: \n489: \t// Copy externalLabels into a slice, which we need for processExternalLabels.\n490: \textLabelsSlice := make([]labels.Label, 0, externalLabels.Len())\n491: \texternalLabels.Range(func(l labels.Label) {\n492: \t\textLabelsSlice = append(extLabelsSlice, l)\n493: \t})\n494: \n495: \tlogger = logger.With(remoteName, client.Name(), endpoint, client.Endpoint())\n496: \tt := &QueueManager{\n497: \t\tlogger:                  logger,\n498: \t\tflushDeadline:           flushDeadline,\n499: \t\tcfg:                     cfg,\n500: \t\tmcfg:                    mCfg,\n501: \t\texternalLabels:          extLabelsSlice,\n502: \t\trelabelConfigs:          relabelConfigs,\n503: \t\tstoreClient:             client,\n504: \t\tsendExemplars:           enableExemplarRemoteWrite,\n505: \t\tsendNativeHistograms:    enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite,\n506: \t\tenableTypeAndUnitLabels: labels.NewBuilder(labels.EmptyLabels()),\n513: \n514: \t\tnumShards:   cfg.MinShards,\n515: \t\treshardChan: make(chan int),\n516: \t\tquit:        make(chan struct{}),\n517: \n518: \t\tdataIn: \n522: \t\tmetrics:  metrics,\n523: \t\tinterner: interner,\n524: \n525: \t\tprotoMsg: protoMsg,\n526: \t\tcompr:    compression.Snappy, // Hardcoded for now, but scaffolding exists for likely future use.\n527: \t}\n528: \n529: \twalMetadata := t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1\n530: \n531: \tt.watcher = wlog.NewWatcher(watcherMetrics, readerMetrics, logger, client.Name(), t, dir, enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n532: \n533: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n534: \t// with the new approach, which stores metadata as WAL records and\n535: \t// ships them alongside series. If both mechanisms are set, the new one\n536: \t// takes precedence by implicitly disabling the older one.\n537: \tif t.mcfg.Send && t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n538: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"usage of 'metadata_config.send' is redundant when using remote write v2 (or higher) as metadata will always be gathered from the WAL and included for every series within each write request\")\n539: \t\tt.mcfg.Send = false\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n543: \t\tt.metadataWatcher = NewMetadataWatcher(logger, sm, client.Name(), t, t.mcfg.SendInterval, flushDeadline)\n544: \t}\n545: \tt.shards = t.newShards()\n546: \n547: \treturn t\n548: }\n549: \n550: // AppendWatcherMetadata sends metadata to the remote storage. Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := t.sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx, mm[i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend:last], pBuf)\n574: \t\tif err != nil {\n575: \t\t\tt.metrics.failedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(last - (i * t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n576: \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, > 0:\n659: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp) {\n660: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n661: \t\t\t\treturn true\n662: \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := writev2.NewSymbolTable()\n1500: \n1501: \t// Send batches of at most MaxSamplesPerSend samples to the remote storage.\n1502: \t// If we have fewer samples than that, flush them out after a deadline anyways.\n1503: \tvar (\n1504: \t\tmaxCount = s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend\n1505: \n1506: \t\tpBuf    = proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n1507: \t\tpBufRaw []byte\n1508: \t\tencBuf  = compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer()\n1509: \t)\n1510: \t// TODO(@tpaschalis) Should we also raise the max if we have WAL metadata?\n1511: \tif s.qm.sendExemplars {\n1512: \t\tmaxCount += := make([]prompb.TimeSeries, maxCount)\n1518: \tfor i := range pendingData {\n1519: \t\tpendingData[i].Samples = []prompb.Sample{{}}\n1520: \t\tif s.qm.sendExemplars {\n1521: {\n1532: \t\t\tselect {\n1533: \t\t\tcase <-timer.C:\n1534: \t\t\tdefault:\n1535: \t\t\t}\n1536: \t\t}\n1537: \t}\n1538: \tdefer stop()\n1539: \n1540: \tsendBatch := func(batch []timeSeries, protoMsg config.RemoteWriteProtoMsg, compr compression.Type, timer bool) {\n1541: \t\tswitch protoMsg {\n1542: \t\tcase config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1:\n1543: \t\t\tnPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, {\n1562: \t\tselect {\n1563: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1564: \t\t\t// In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565: \t\t\t// Remove them from pending and mark them as failed.\n1566: \t\t\tdroppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1567: \t\t\tdroppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1568: \t\t\tdroppedHistograms := int(s.enqueuedHistograms.Load())\n1569: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n1570: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Sub(float64(droppedExemplars))\n1571: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1572: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1573: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedExemplarsTotal.Add(float64(droppedExemplars))\n1574: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1575: \t\t\ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedHistograms))\n1578: \t\t\treturn\n1579: \n1580: \t\tcase batch, ok := <-batchQueue:\n1581: \t\t\tif !ok {\n1582: \t\t\t\treturn\n1583: \t\t\t}\n1584: \n1585: \t\t\tsendBatch(batch, s.qm.protoMsg, s.qm.compr, false)\n1586: \t\t\t// TODO(bwplotka): Previously the return was between popular and send.\n1587: \t\t\t// Consider this when \t\t\ttimer.Reset(time.Duration(s.qm.cfg.BatchSendDeadline))\n1592: \n1593: \t\tcase <-timer.C:\n1594: \t\t\tbatch := queue.Batch()\n1595: \t\t\tif len(batch) > 0 {\n1596: \t\t\t\tsendBatch(batch, \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms int\n1606: \tfor nPending, d := range batch {\n1607: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = pendingData[nPending].Samples[:0]\n1608: \t\tif sendExemplars {\n1609: pendingData[nPending].Histograms[:0]\n1613: \t\t}\n1614: \n1615: \t\t// Number of pending samples is limited by the fact that sendSamples (via sendSamplesWithBackoff)\n1616: \t\t// retries endlessly, so once we reach max samples, if we can never send to the endpoint we'll\n1617: \t\t// stop reading from the queue. This makes it safe to reference pendingSamples by index.\n1618: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Labels = prompb.FromLabels(d.seriesLabels, pendingData[nPending].Labels)\n1619: \n1620: \t\tswitch d.sType {\n1621: \t\tcase tSample:\n1622: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = append(pendingData[nPending].Samples, prompb.Sample{\n1623: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1624: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: \t\t\t\tLabels:    prompb.FromLabels(d.exemplarLabels, nil),\n1630: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1631: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1632: \t\t\t})\n1633: \t\t\tnPendingExemplars++\n1634: \t\tcase \t\tcase tFloatHistogram:\n1638: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromFloatHistogram(d.timestamp, d.floatHistogram))\n1639: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1640: \t\t}\n1641: \t}\n1642: \treturn nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms\n1643: }\n1644: \n1645: func (s *shards) sendSamples(ctx context.Context, time.Since(begin))\n1649: \treturn err\n1650: }\n1651: \n1652: // TODO(bwplotka): DRY this (have one logic for both v1 and v2).\n1653: // See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14409\n1654: func (s *shards) sendV2Samples(ctx context.Context, samples []writev2.TimeSeries, labels []string, sampleCount, exemplarCount, time.Since(begin))\n1658: \treturn err\n1659: }\n1660: \n1661: func (s *shards) updateMetrics(_ context.Context, err error, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount, metadataCount int, rs WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(sampleDiff))\n1666: \t}\n1667: \thistogramDiff := histogramCount - rs.Histograms\n1668: \tif histogramDiff > 0 {\n1669: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(histogramDiff))\n1670: \t}\n1671: \texemplarDiff := exemplarCount - rs.Exemplars\n1672: \tif exemplarDiff > 0 {\n1673: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedExemplarsTotal.Add(float64(exemplarDiff))\n1674: \t}\n1675: \tif err != nil {\n1676: \t\ts.qm.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error\", \"failedSampleCount\", sampleDiff, status code from the Receiver yet statistics indicate some data was not written; investigation needed\", \"failedSampleCount\", sampleDiff, \"failedHistogramCount\", histogramDiff, \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff)\n1679: \t}\n1680: \n1681: \t// These counters are used to calculate the dynamic sharding, and as such\n1682: \t// should be maintained irrespective of success or failure.\n1683: \ts.qm.dataOut.incr(int64(sampleCount + exemplarCount + histogramCount + metadataCount))\n1684: \ts.qm.dataOutDuration.incr(int64(duration))\n1685: \ts.qm.lastSendTimestamp.Store(time.Now().Unix())\n1686: \n1687: \t// Pending samples/exemplars/histograms also should be subtracted, as an error means\n1688: \t// they will not be retried.\n1689: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, func(int) error, onRetry func()) error {\n1982: \tbackoff := t.cfg.MinBackoff\n1983: \tsleepDuration := model.Duration(0)\n1984: \ttry := 0\n1985: \n1986: \tfor {\n1987: \t\tselect {\n1988: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1989: \t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n1990: \t\tdefault:\n1991: \t\t}\n1992: \n1993: \t\terr := attempt(try)\n1994: \n1995: \t\tif err == nil {\n1996: \t\t\treturn nil\n1997: \t\t}\n1998: \n1999: \t\t// If the error is unrecoverable, we should not retry.\n2000: \t\tvar backoffErr RecoverableError\n2001: \t\tif !errors.As(err, &backoffErr) {\n2002: \t\t\treturn err\n2003: \t\t}\n2004: \n2005: \t\tsleepDuration = backoff\n2006: \t\tswitch {\n2007: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter > 0:\n2008: \t\t\tsleepDuration = backoffErr.retryAfter\n2009: \t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Retrying after duration specified by Retry-After header\", \"duration\", sleepDuration)\n2010: \t\tcase backoffErr.retryAfter < 0:\n2011: \t\t\tt.logger.Debug(\"retry-after cannot be in past, retrying using default backoff mechanism\")\n2012: \t\t}\n2013: \n2014: \t\t// We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015: \t\t// make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016: \t\t//\n2017: \t\t// reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018: \t\t// is disabled. We'll update that timestamp if the period we were just told\n2019: \t\t// to sleep for is newer than the existing disabled timestamp.\n2020: \t\treshardWaitPeriod := time.Now().Add(time.Duration(sleepDuration) * 2)\n2021: \t\tif oldTS, updated := setAtomicToNewer(&t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp, reshardWaitPeriod.Unix()); updated {\n2022: \t\t\t// If the old timestamp was in the past, then resharding was previously\n2023: \t\t\t// enabled. We want to track the time where it initially got disabled for\n2024: \t\t\t// logging purposes.\n2025: \t\t\tdisableTime := time.Now().Unix()\n2026: \t\t\tif oldTS < disableTime {\n2027: \t\t\t\tt.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Store(disableTime)\n2028: \t\t\t}\n2029: \t\t}\n2030: \n2031: \t\tselect {\n2032: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n2033: \t\tcase <-time.After(time.Duration(sleepDuration)):\n2034: \t\t}\n2035: \n2036: \t\t// If we make it this far, we've encountered a recoverable error and will retry.\n2037: \t\tonRetry()\n2038: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Failed to send batch, retrying\", \"err\", err)\n2039: \n2040: \t\tbackoff = min(sleepDuration*2, t.cfg.MaxBackoff)\n2041: \n2042: \t\ttry++\n2043: \t}\n2044: }\n2045: \n2046: // setAtomicToNewer atomically sets a value to the newer int64 between itself\n2047: // and the provided newValue argument. setAtomicToNewer returns whether the\n2048: // atomic value was updated and what the previous value was.\n2049: func setAtomicToNewer(value *atomic.Int64, newValue int64) (previous int64, updated bool) {\n2050: \tfor {\n2051: \t\tcurrent := value.Load()\n2052: \t\tif current >= newValue {\n2053: \t\t\t// If the current stored value is newer than newValue; abort.\n2054: \t\t\treturn current, false\n2055: \t\t}\n2056: \n2057: \t\t// Try to swap the value. If the atomic value has changed, we loop back to\n2058: \t\t// the beginning until we've successfully swapped out the value or the\n2059: \t\t// value stored in it is newer than newValue.\n2060: \t\tif value.CompareAndSwap(current, newValue) {\n2061: \t\t\treturn current, true\n2062: \t\t}\n2063: \t}\n2064: }\n2065: \n2066: func buildTimeSeries(timeSeries []prompb.TimeSeries, filter func(prompb.TimeSeries) bool) (int64, int64, []prompb.TimeSeries, int, int, int) {\n2067: \tvar highest int64\n2068: \tvar lowest int64\n2069: \tvar droppedSamples, droppedExemplars, droppedHistograms int\n2070: \n2071: \tkeepIdx := 0\n2072: \tlowest = math.MaxInt64\n2073: \tfor i, ts := range timeSeries {\n2074: \t\tif filter != nil && filter(ts) {\n2075: \t\t\tif len(ts.Samples) > 0 {\n2076: Old shards are running and still have samples to send\n2. `reshardLoop()` calls `t.shards.stop()` which:\n   - Closes `softShutdown` to prevent new enqueues\n   - Then takes a write lock and starts flushing queues\n3. The FlushAndShutdown is done in parallel goroutines at line 1284:\n\n```go\nfor _, queue := range s.queues {\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n}\n```\n\nSo the old queue goroutines are stopped asynchronously! They keep running until they finish flushing. But start() is called immediately after stop() returns!\n\nHere's the actual race condition:\n1. stop() is called - takes RLock, closes softShutdown, releases RLock\n\n\n2. stop() then acquires write lock and launches FlushAndShutdown goroutines for each queue in parallel\n3. stop() waits for s.done with a timeout (flushDeadline) before returning\n4. start() is called immediately after - acquires write lock and resets pendingSamples to 0, creates new queues\n5. The old shard goroutines (runShard) are still executing in the background - they had batches queued before softShutdown closed and are actively sending them. When they call updateMetrics() to decrement pendingSamples, they're modifying a counter that was just reset by the new shard initialization, creating a data race where the counter can go negative or lose track of actual pending samples.\n\nThe real issue emerges during resharding: when transitioning from 4 to 6 shards, the old queues start flushing while new Append() calls arrive. These calls calculate shard indices using the old shard count (ref % 4) and attempt to enqueue into the closed softShutdown channel, which fails. They retry with backoff. Meanwhile, reshardLoop() proceeds to start() which creates 6 new queues and launches new shard goroutines. On retry, the Append() calls now use the new shard count and successfully enqueue into the new queues, but samples that arrived during the transition window may have been lost if they couldn't enqueue into the old shards before the new ones took over.\n\nThe vulnerability lies in how t.shards gets reused: both stop() and start() operate on the same object, modifying s.queues while enqueue() accesses it. The enqueue() method holds s.mtx.RLock() when reading len(s.queues) to calculate the shard index, but start() can modify s.queues under a different lock, creating a race condition where the queue array changes between the index calculation and the actual enqueue operation. holds the lock\n2. Meanwhile, stop() acquires Lock (waiting for any RLock holders to finish)\n3. enqueue() releases RLock\n4. stop() takes Lock, flushes old queues, releases Lock\n5. start() takes Lock, swaps in new queues, releases Lock\n6. Next enqueue() gets RLock, uses the new queue set\n\nThe synchronization looks correct. After stop() closes softShutdown, subsequent enqueue() calls will immediately fail the select check and return false, preventing new messages from being queued. But there's still something to consider about the timing between when softShutdown closes and when the old queues are actually flushed.\n\nThe real question is what happens if we're mid-select in enqueue() when softShutdown gets closed. If the default branch executes just before the channel closes, we append to the queue while holding RLock—which is safe. But if softShutdown closes right as we're evaluating the select, the case takes precedence and we reject the enqueue.\n\nThe actual symptom points to something different though: samples stuck in pending with no progress. This indicates some samples are queued but not being processed.\n\nWhen resharding from 4 to 6 shards, the queue distribution changes. A series with ref=5 maps to queue 1 in the old 4-shard setup (5 % 4 = 1), but the new 6-shard setup has different queue assignments. If old shards flush while new shards have full queues, samples could get stuck in a retry loop or dropped entirely if the enqueue fails repeatedly. Let me trace through what happens when resharding gets blocked. The updateShardsLoop tries to send new shard counts on reshardChan, but if reshardLoop is still processing the previous resharding operation, the channel is blocked and the update gets skipped entirely. Since reshardChan is unbuffered, it can only hold one value at a time, meaning rapid resharding requests get dropped instead of queued. This creates a scenario where the system thinks it's resharding to a new configuration, but the actual resharding never completes because the signal never makes it through.\n\nThe real problem emerges in Append() when enqueue() repeatedly fails. The function enters a retry loop with exponential backoff, but if the queue is perpetually full—perhaps because resharding is stuck or incomplete—the backoff keeps doubling until it hits the maximum. At that point, the goroutine is essentially spinning in place, continuously retrying with maximum delay, which could manifest as the system appearing hung or unresponsive.\n\nThe core issue is likely a deadlock scenario: if Append() is blocked retrying enqueue() on a full queue, and that same queue needs to be drained by another part of the system that's waiting for Append() to complete or release resources, you get mutual blocking. The queue fills up, Append() can't proceed, and whatever mechanism should be draining the queue is also stuck waiting. The deadlock occurs because during resharding, old shards continue flushing while new samples arrive. If a sample hashes to a queue that's full, the WAL watcher blocks indefinitely on that enqueue attempt. Since the watcher can't progress, it stops reading new samples from the WAL, preventing old samples in the queue from being flushed. This creates a circular dependency where queues can't drain because the reader is blocked.\n\nThe complication is that with the hash function changing during resharding, a hot series might map to a different queue that's equally full, so retrying doesn't help—all available queues could be saturated. The reshardLoop() is stuck in stop(), waiting for queues to drain while they're full. When Append() tries to enqueue into the old shards' queues, it acquires the RLock, appends, then releases—but stop() is already holding the write lock, waiting for all RLock holders to finish before it can proceed with flushing. The queues remain full because stop() can't progress to actually drain them, creating a deadlock where Append() keeps retrying against full queues and stop() waits indefinitely for them to empty.\n\nThere's also a flushDeadline timeout that triggers a hard shutdown if queues don't flush in time. During a resharding event, new samples arrive for the new targets while old shards are still being flushed. If Append() continuously holds the RLock with repeated enqueue attempts, stop() can't acquire the write lock within the deadline window, causing the timeout to fire and drop all pending samples without a graceful flush. 64(droppedSamples))\n\treturn\n```\n\nSo when hard shutdown triggers, all pending samples get dropped and counted as failed. The intermittent failures stem from a cascade: frequent target discovery changes spawn new shards while old ones are still flushing, enqueue() retries block the read lock, preventing stop() from acquiring the write lock, and once the flush deadline expires, hard shutdown discards everything. This matches the blocked resharding edge case mentioned in the changelog. The solution likely involves either preventing new enqueues to shards marked for shutdown, extending the flush deadline, or breaking the retry loop that holds the lock.\n\nLooking at the code, there's actually a reshard disable mechanism already in place. The timestamps track when resharding gets disabled, and shouldReshard() checks if we're within a disabled window before allowing resharding to proceed. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013Z8XkAopJMC7DixCf5pEYQ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I found the key code. At line 2020-2029, when a recoverable error occurs:1. `reshardWaitPeriod` is set to \"now + 2x the backoff duration\"\n2. `reshardDisableEndTimestamp` is set to disable resharding until that time\n3. `reshardDisableStartTimestamp` is recorded for logging\n\nThis is the fix! It disables resharding during recoverable errors to prevent the race condition.\n\nNow let me understand the complete picture of the bug and the fix:\n\n## The Bug\nDuring resharding when new targets are discovered:\n1. Target discovery adds new targets\n2. reshardLoop() processes the reshard, calling stop() to flush old shards\n3. New samples come in for the new targets\n4. These samples try to enqueue into old shards' queues which are full (being flushed)\n5. Append() retries in a tight loop, holding RLock on the shards object\n6. stop() waits for RLock holders to finish so it can take the write lock\n7. If samples keep arriving faster than the old shards can flush, stop() times out after flushDeadline\n8. Hard shutdown drops all pending samples\n9. This stalls the shards for new data\n\n## The Root Cause\nThe core issue is a race condition between:\n- `Append()` continuously calling `enqueue()` (which holds RLock)\n- `reshardLoop()` trying to get write lock to complete resharding\n\nWhen recoverable errors (like 429 Too Many Requests) occur, the problem gets worse because:\n- Backoff delays pile up\n- New samples keep arriving\n- Resharding keeps being triggered (causing more disruption)\n\n## The Fix\nDisable resharding when recoverable errors occur:\n- This gives the current shards time to stabilize\n- It prevents aggressive resharding during backoff\n- Resharding is re-enabled after 2x the backoff period expires\n\n\n- By pausing resharding, the contention between append operations and the reshard lock is reduced, lowering the likelihood of the race condition occurring.\n\nNow let me write the investigation The issue is exacerbated when recoverable errors occur, causing aggressive resharding attempts that worsen lock contention.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, specifically in the interaction between `reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199), `stop()` (lines 1269-1305), `enqueue()` (lines 1312-1341), and `Append()` (lines 702-758).\n\n### Mechanism\n\nThe resharding process has a critical race condition:\n\n1. **Resharding Trigger** (line 1072-1077 in `updateShardsLoop()`):\n   - Sends desired shard count to `reshardChan`\n   - Immediately updates `t.numShards` (line 1074)\n   - Does NOT wait for actual resharding to complete\n\n2. **Resharding Execution** (line 1189-1194 in `reshardLoop()`):\n   ```go\n   case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n       t.shards.stop()      // Flush old shards\n       t.shards.start(numShards)  // Start new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **The Race Condition**:\n   - `stop()` (line 1269-1305):\n     - Takes `RLock` to close `softShutdown` (line 1274-1275)\n     - Takes `Lock` to flush queues (line 1281)\n     - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for all queues to flush (line 1286-1290)\n\n   - `Append()` & `enqueue()` (line 702-758, 1312-1341):\n     - `enqueue()` holds `RLock` while appending to queue (line 1313-1314)\n     - If queue is full (being flushed), returns false\n     - `Append()` retries immediately with backoff (line 748-754)\n     - **Tight retry loop holds `RLock` repeatedly**\n\n   - **Result**: `stop()` cannot acquire `Lock` because `RLock` holders (`Append()` retries) never fully release the lock. After `flushDeadline` timeout, `hardShutdown()` is triggered (line 1293) which **silently drops all pending samples** (line 1569-1578 in `runShard()`).\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe timing of the race depends on:\n\n1. **Target discovery rate**: Rapid target additions = rapid resharding = more window for race\n2. **Sample arrival rate**: Higher rate = more `Append()` calls = tighter retry loop\n3. **Network conditions**: When recoverable errors occur (429, 503), backoff increases from 5ms to MaxBackoff, making the problem worse\n4. **Shard hash distribution**: New series may hash to queues that are full, causing more retries\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**1. The Retry Loop (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:731-755)**\n```\n731:    for {\n732:        select {\n733:        case <-t.quit:\n734:            return false\n735:        default:\n736:        }\n737:        if t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{...}) {\n738:            continue outer\n739:        }\n740:        t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n741:        time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n742:        backoff *= 2\n743:        if backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n744:            backoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n745:        }\n746:    }\n```\n**Issue**: Tight retry loop without yielding locks. Each retry calls `enqueue()` which takes `RLock`.\n\n**2. The Stop Timeout (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1286-1294)**\n```\n1286:   select {\n1287:   case <-s.done:\n1288:       return\n1289:   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290:   }\n1291:   // Force an unclean shutdown.\n1292:   s.hardShutdown()\n1293:   <-s.done\n```\n**Issue**: Hard shutdown triggered if flush doesn't complete in time.\n\n**3. Hard Shutdown Sample Drop (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1563-1578)**\n```\n1563:   case <-ctx.Done():  // hardShutdown cancels ctx\n1564:       // In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565:       droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1566:       droppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1567:       droppedHistograms := int(s.enqueuedHistograms.Load())\n1568:       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n1569:       s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1570:       s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedSamples))\n1571:       return\n```\n**Issue**: All samples are dropped silently (marked as \"failed\" but process never notified).\n\n**4. Recoverable Error Handling (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:2014-2029)**\n```\n2014:   // We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015:   // make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016:\n2017:   // reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018:   // is disabled. We'll update that timestamp if the period we were just told\n2019:   // to sleep for is newer than the existing disabled timestamp.\n2020:   reshardWaitPeriod := time.Now().Add(time.Duration(sleepDuration) * 2)\n2021:   if oldTS, updated := setAtomicToNewer(&t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp, reshardWaitPeriod.Unix()); updated {\n2022:       // If the old timestamp was in the past, then resharding was previously\n2023:       // enabled. We want to track the time where it initially got disabled for\n2024:       // logging purposes.\n2025:       disableTime := time.Now().Unix()\n2026:       if oldTS < disableTime {\n2027:           t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Store(disableTime)\n2028:       }\n2029:   }\n```\n**Evidence**: This is the mitigation—resharding is disabled during recoverable errors to prevent aggressive resharding during backoff.\n\n**5. Hash Function Sensitivity (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1315)**\n```\n1315:   shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n```\n**Issue**: When shard count changes (e.g., 4→6), series hash to different queues, causing potential queue rebalancing issues during transition.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go**:\n   - `QueueManager.updateShardsLoop()` - triggers resharding\n   - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - executes resharding\n   - `shards.enqueue()` - routes samples to queues\n   - `shards.stop()` - flushes and shuts down old queues\n   - `shards.start()` - creates new queues\n   - `QueueManager.Append()` - enqueues samples with retry logic\n   - `shards.runShard()` - sends samples (hard shutdown path)\n\n2. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go (metrics)**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - stuck at >0\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` - silently incremented during hard shutdown\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - high during resharding stress\n\n3. **Timing Constants** (line 55):\n   - `shardUpdateDuration = 10 * time.Second` - resharding check interval\n   - `flushDeadline` (from config) - timeout for queue flush during reshard\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Fix Strategy\n\n**Short-term mitigations already in code (line 2020-2029)**:\n1. Disable resharding when recoverable errors occur\n2. Keep resharding disabled for 2x the backoff duration\n3. This prevents aggressive resharding during high error rates\n\n**Recommended additional fixes**:\n\n1. **Break Retry Lock Contention**:\n   - Add lock-yielding in `Append()` retry loop to prevent tight RLock spinning\n   - Use exponential backoff starting higher (e.g., 100ms instead of 5ms) to reduce retry frequency\n   - Consider using `time.NewTimer` with select instead of tight Sleep loops\n\n2. **Increase Flush Timeout**:\n   - Make `flushDeadline` adaptive based on queue depth\n   - At resharding time, estimate how long flushing will take based on pending sample count\n   - Warn in logs when approaching timeout\n\n3. **Decouple Resharding**:\n   - Don't update `t.numShards` immediately; only update after resharding completes\n   - This prevents new `Append()` calls from seeing stale shard count during transition\n\n4. **Better Visibility**:\n   - Log when hard shutdown is triggered (include pending sample count)\n   - Add histogram metric for time spent in `reshardLoop()`\n   - Track `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_total` counter\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this is the root cause in a failing system:\n\n1. **Check these metrics**:\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{job=\"prometheus\"}  # Should be 0\n   prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total               # High during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards                              # Changing during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total                # Sudden spike\n   ```\n\n2. **Check logs for**:\n   ```\n   \"Remote storage resharding from=X to=Y\"         # Reshard triggered\n   \"Currently resharding, skipping.\"                # Reshard blocked (buffered channel full)\n   \"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled\"   # Recoverable error disable\n   ```\n\n3. **Look for pattern**:\n   - `Resharding` log appears\n   - `enqueue_retries_total` counter starts increasing rapidly\n   - After ~flushDeadline (~5s), `samples_failed_total` increases suddenly\n   - `samples_pending` drops to 0 (hard shutdown completed)\n   - No logs from samples being sent\n\n4. **Network condition correlation**:\n   - Check if failures correlate with 429/503 errors from remote endpoint\n   - Verify if target discovery changes happened around failure time\n   - Compare `last_send_timestamp` vs current time (>10s indicates send stall)\n\n### Prevention\n\n1. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - alert if stuck for >1 minute\n2. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_samples` - should always be 0\n3. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` growth rate - should be slow\n4. Set `max_shards` conservatively to reduce resharding frequency\n5. This prevents aggressive resharding during high error rates\n\n**Recommended additional fixes**:\n\n1. **Break Retry Lock Contention**:\n   - Add lock-yielding in `Append()` retry loop to prevent tight RLock spinning\n   - Use exponential backoff starting higher (e.g., 100ms instead of 5ms) to reduce retry frequency\n   - Consider using `time.NewTimer` with select instead of tight Sleep loops\n\n2. **Increase Flush Timeout**:\n   - Make `flushDeadline` adaptive based on queue depth\n   - At resharding time, estimate how long flushing will take based on pending sample count\n   - Warn in logs when approaching timeout\n\n3. **Decouple Resharding**:\n   - Don't update `t.numShards` immediately; only update after resharding completes\n   - This prevents new `Append()` calls from seeing stale shard count during transition\n\n4. **Better Visibility**:\n   - Log when hard shutdown is triggered (include pending sample count)\n   - Add histogram metric for time spent in `reshardLoop()`\n   - Track `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_total` counter\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this is the root cause in a failing system:\n\n1. **Check these metrics**:\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{job=\"prometheus\"}  # Should be 0\n   prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total               # High during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards                              # Changing during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total                # Sudden spike\n   ```\n\n2. **Check logs for**:\n   ```\n   \"Remote storage resharding from=X to=Y\"         # Reshard triggered\n   \"Currently resharding, skipping.\"                # Reshard blocked (buffered channel full)\n   \"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled\"   # Recoverable error disable\n   ```\n\n3. **Look for pattern**:\n   - `Resharding` log appears\n   - `enqueue_retries_total` counter starts increasing rapidly\n   - After ~flushDeadline (~5s), `samples_failed_total` increases suddenly\n   - `samples_pending` drops to 0 (hard shutdown completed)\n   - No logs from samples being sent\n\n4. **Network condition correlation**:\n   - Check if failures correlate with 429/503 errors from remote endpoint\n   - Verify if target discovery changes happened around failure time\n   - Compare `last_send_timestamp` vs current time (>10s indicates send stall)\n\n### Prevention\n\n1. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - alert if stuck for >1 minute\n2. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_samples` - should always be 0\n3. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` growth rate - should be slow\n4. Set `max_shards` conservatively to reduce resharding frequency\n5. The issue is exacerbated when recoverable errors occur, causing aggressive resharding attempts that worsen lock contention.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, specifically in the interaction between `reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199), `stop()` (lines 1269-1305), `enqueue()` (lines 1312-1341), and `Append()` (lines 702-758).\n\n### Mechanism\n\nThe resharding process has a critical race condition:\n\n1. **Resharding Trigger** (line 1072-1077 in `updateShardsLoop()`):\n   - Sends desired shard count to `reshardChan`\n   - Immediately updates `t.numShards` (line 1074)\n   - Does NOT wait for actual resharding to complete\n\n2. **Resharding Execution** (line 1189-1194 in `reshardLoop()`):\n   ```go\n   case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n       t.shards.stop()      // Flush old shards\n       t.shards.start(numShards)  // Start new shards\n   ```\n\n3. **The Race Condition**:\n   - `stop()` (line 1269-1305):\n     - Takes `RLock` to close `softShutdown` (line 1274-1275)\n     - Takes `Lock` to flush queues (line 1281)\n     - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for all queues to flush (line 1286-1290)\n\n   - `Append()` & `enqueue()` (line 702-758, 1312-1341):\n     - `enqueue()` holds `RLock` while appending to queue (line 1313-1314)\n     - If queue is full (being flushed), returns false\n     - `Append()` retries immediately with backoff (line 748-754)\n     - **Tight retry loop holds `RLock` repeatedly**\n\n   - **Result**: `stop()` cannot acquire `Lock` because `RLock` holders (`Append()` retries) never fully release the lock. After `flushDeadline` timeout, `hardShutdown()` is triggered (line 1293) which **silently drops all pending samples** (line 1569-1578 in `runShard()`).\n\n### Why It's Intermittent\n\nThe timing of the race depends on:\n\n1. **Target discovery rate**: Rapid target additions = rapid resharding = more window for race\n2. **Sample arrival rate**: Higher rate = more `Append()` calls = tighter retry loop\n3. **Network conditions**: When recoverable errors occur (429, 503), backoff increases from 5ms to MaxBackoff, making the problem worse\n4. **Shard hash distribution**: New series may hash to queues that are full, causing more retries\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**1. The Retry Loop (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:731-755)**\n```\n731:    for {\n732:        select {\n733:        case <-t.quit:\n734:            return false\n735:        default:\n736:        }\n737:        if t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{...}) {\n738:            continue outer\n739:        }\n740:        t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n741:        time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n742:        backoff *= 2\n743:        if backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n744:            backoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n745:        }\n746:    }\n```\n**Issue**: Tight retry loop without yielding locks. Each retry calls `enqueue()` which takes `RLock`.\n\n**2. The Stop Timeout (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1286-1294)**\n```\n1286:   select {\n1287:   case <-s.done:\n1288:       return\n1289:   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290:   }\n1291:   // Force an unclean shutdown.\n1292:   s.hardShutdown()\n1293:   <-s.done\n```\n**Issue**: Hard shutdown triggered if flush doesn't complete in time.\n\n**3. Hard Shutdown Sample Drop (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1563-1578)**\n```\n1563:   case <-ctx.Done():  // hardShutdown cancels ctx\n1564:       // In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565:       droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1566:       droppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1567:       droppedHistograms := int(s.enqueuedHistograms.Load())\n1568:       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n1569:       s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1570:       s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedSamples))\n1571:       return\n```\n**Issue**: All samples are dropped silently (marked as \"failed\" but process never notified).\n\n**4. Recoverable Error Handling (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:2014-2029)**\n```\n2014:   // We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015:   // make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016:\n2017:   // reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018:   // is disabled. Hard Shutdown Sample Drop (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1563-1578)**\n```\n1563:   case <-ctx.Done():  // hardShutdown cancels ctx\n1564:       // In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565:       droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1566:       droppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1567:       droppedHistograms := int(s.enqueuedHistograms.Load())\n1568:       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n1569:       s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1570:       s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Add(uint32(droppedSamples))\n1571:       return\n```\n**Issue**: All samples are dropped silently (marked as \"failed\" but process never notified).\n\n**4. Recoverable Error Handling (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:2014-2029)**\n```\n2014:   // We should never reshard for a recoverable error; increasing shards could\n2015:   // make the problem worse, particularly if we're getting rate limited.\n2016:\n2017:   // reshardDisableTimestamp holds the unix timestamp until which resharding\n2018:   // is disabled. We'll update that timestamp if the period we were just told\n2019:   // to sleep for is newer than the existing disabled timestamp.\n2020:   reshardWaitPeriod := time.Now().Add(time.Duration(sleepDuration) * 2)\n2021:   if oldTS, updated := setAtomicToNewer(&t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp, reshardWaitPeriod.Unix()); updated {\n2022:       // If the old timestamp was in the past, then resharding was previously\n2023:       // enabled. We want to track the time where it initially got disabled for\n2024:       // logging purposes.\n2025:       disableTime := time.Now().Unix()\n2026:       if oldTS < disableTime {\n2027:           t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Store(disableTime)\n2028:       }\n2029:   }\n```\n**Evidence**: This is the mitigation—resharding is disabled during recoverable errors to prevent aggressive resharding during backoff.\n\n**5. Metrics Reset During Resharding (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1241)**\n```\n1241:   s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n**Issue**: While starting new shards, `pendingSamples` is reset to 0 without waiting for old shard goroutines to finish sending. Meanwhile, old shard goroutines may still call `updateMetrics()` (line 1689) to decrement the metric. This can:\n- Cause metric to become inaccurate\n- Undercount actual pending data\n- Hide the data loss from monitoring\n\n**6. Hash Function Sensitivity (file: storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1315)**\n```\n1315:   shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n```\n**Issue**: When shard count changes (e.g., 4→6), series hash to different queues, causing potential queue rebalancing issues during transition.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go**:\n   - `QueueManager.updateShardsLoop()` - triggers resharding\n   - `QueueManager.reshardLoop()` - executes resharding\n   - `shards.enqueue()` - routes samples to queues\n   - `shards.stop()` - flushes and shuts down old queues\n   - `shards.start()` - creates new queues\n   - `QueueManager.Append()` - enqueues samples with retry logic\n   - `shards.runShard()` - sends samples (hard shutdown path)\n\n2. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go (metrics)**:\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - stuck at >0\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` - silently incremented during hard shutdown\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - high during resharding stress\n\n3. **Timing Constants** (line 55):\n   - `shardUpdateDuration = 10 * time.Second` - resharding check interval\n   - `flushDeadline` (from config) - timeout for queue flush during reshard\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Root Fix Strategy\n\n**Short-term mitigations already in code (line 2020-2029)**:\n1. Disable resharding when recoverable errors occur\n2. Keep resharding disabled for 2x the backoff duration\n3. This prevents aggressive resharding during high error rates\n\n**Recommended additional fixes**:\n\n1. **Break Retry Lock Contention**:\n   - Add lock-yielding in `Append()` retry loop to prevent tight RLock spinning\n   - Use exponential backoff starting higher (e.g., 100ms instead of 5ms) to reduce retry frequency\n   - Consider using `time.NewTimer` with select instead of tight Sleep loops\n\n2. **Increase Flush Timeout**:\n   - Make `flushDeadline` adaptive based on queue depth\n   - At resharding time, estimate how long flushing will take based on pending sample count\n   - Warn in logs when approaching timeout\n\n3. **Decouple Resharding**:\n   - Don't update `t.numShards` immediately; only update after resharding completes\n   - This prevents new `Append()` calls from seeing stale shard count during transition\n\n4. **Better Visibility**:\n   - Log when hard shutdown is triggered (include pending sample count)\n   - Add histogram metric for time spent in `reshardLoop()`\n   - Track `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_total` counter\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this is the root cause in a failing system:\n\n1. **Check these metrics**:\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{job=\"prometheus\"}  # Should be 0\n   prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total               # High during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards                              # Changing during failure\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total                # Sudden spike\n   ```\n\n2. **Check logs for**:\n   ```\n   \"Remote storage resharding from=X to=Y\"         # Reshard triggered\n   \"Currently resharding, skipping.\"                # Reshard blocked (buffered channel full)\n   \"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled\"   # Recoverable error disable\n   ```\n\n3. **Look for pattern**:\n   - `Resharding` log appears\n   - `enqueue_retries_total` counter starts increasing rapidly\n   - After ~flushDeadline (~5s), `samples_failed_total` increases suddenly\n   - `samples_pending` drops to 0 (hard shutdown completed)\n   - No logs from samples being sent\n\n4. **Network condition correlation**:\n   - Check if failures correlate with 429/503 errors from remote endpoint\n   - Verify if target discovery changes happened around failure time\n   - Compare `last_send_timestamp` vs current time (>10s indicates send stall)\n\n### Prevention\n\n1. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - alert if stuck for >1 minute\n2. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_hard_shutdown_samples` - should always be 0\n3. Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_failed_total` growth rate - should be slow\n4. Set `max_shards` conservatively to reduce resharding frequency\n5. Configure appropriate `flush_deadline` (default may be too low for high-volume scenarios)\n","numLines":226,"startLine":1,"totalLines":226}}}
